Women's Special Issue

Cotton Yarn: The Yarn Market's Ordinary Fluctuations are Limited

The yarn market is calm, the situation is stable, and it will probably remain in a state of fluctuation. However, yarn merchants' sales are still healthy, and confidence is good. There is still a tendency among the industry to reduce yarn holdings, leaning towards multiple directions. However, when prices rise sharply, foreign firms also release their holdings, so the market enters a state of hovering.

Gold Rooster Barely Five Cents

In the opening session of the cotton yarn exchange, following the momentum from the previous day, prices continued to rise by five cents this month. However, as the trading progressed to distant months, the market became peaceful and remained static. Trading volume was sparse, with buyers and sellers evenly matched. After the second session, the market weakened. Wang Taixing, Rui Da, Geng Feng, and Fu Kang did not sell, prices gradually declining, but the drop was very slight. By the close, it was reported that there were still over eight hundred bales of spot yarn traded. The market slightly rebounded a few cents. Jin Chang, He Xing, Chang Yu, and Shen Ji bought in. As a result, all months closed down by three, four, or five cents compared to the previous day's close. The afternoon session opened well, but the second and third sessions declined again. Trading was very narrow, and sentiment was ordinary. By the close, due to still substantial spot yarn business, there was a slight rebound. As a result, prices for all months were similar to the morning close. Sales were reported as Yu Ji 1,150 bales, Heng Yi 1,450 bales, Da Feng 1,450 bales, Zhen Da 1,200 bales, Geng Feng 1,450 bales, Rui Da 1,350 bales, Wang Taixing 1,500 bales, Fu Kang 1,000 bales, and Tong He 800 bales. Purchases were He Yu 2,750 bales, Jin Chang 1,100 bales, Yu Da 900 bales, Xing Chang 1,350 bales, Chang Yu 1,100 bales, Shen Ji 1,400 bales, Xin Cheng 900 bales, and Tai Chang 800 bales. The daily high and low prices are listed on the left.

Spot Yarn Sales Still Good

A total of 1,512 bales were traded throughout the day, with selling prices similar to the previous day. The purchase volume for each group is listed below:

Tianjin 200 Guangdong 300 Shantou 40

Inland 730 Changsha 10 Yunnan 40

Xiamen 5 Nanjing 2 Hankou 155

New Cotton Shipments Not Yet Smooth

The cotton market is stable, mainly because the supply from various sources is not abundant, and factories are still eager for new cotton. Shipments from production areas are not smooth due to the firm and high selling prices of spot cotton. Recent short covering activity has pushed up market prices. However, overseas cotton markets are ordinary.

Recent Short Covering Especially Active

In the opening session of the cotton exchange, due to a slight increase in American cotton of one to five points and mixed Indian cotton with fluctuations between 0.25 and 0.75 rupees, and a decline in Osaka's Sanpin cotton of 1.5 to 2 cents, market sentiment was mediocre. Prices for various months were mixed, fluctuating by five points. However, later Heng Yi, Rui Da, Da Feng, Xin Cheng, Sheng Yuan, Tong He, and Da Chang started selling, causing a mid-session drop of ten to one cent. By the third close, because factories were vigorously seeking new cotton and there were no surplus arrivals, a certain person shorted October cotton, causing it to rise, pulling up distant months. Da Fu, He Xing, Xin Chang, Ju Xing, Feng Tai, Shen Ji, Yong Da, and others also bought heavily. As a result, prices for various months rose or fell by five points to 1.5 cents compared to the previous day's close. The afternoon session opened with an unusually calm market and very little trading. As a result, prices for various months fell by one to 1.5 cents compared to the morning close. Sales were Heng Yi 4,800 piculs, Da Feng 3,300 piculs, Zhen Da 1,900 piculs, Chang Ji 1,200 piculs, Rui Da 7,400 piculs, Chang Feng 1,200 piculs, Da Chang 1,300 piculs, Tong He 7,600 piculs, Yuan Xing Chang 1,100 piculs, Xie Cheng 1,000 piculs, and Tong Ji 1,000 piculs. Purchases were Da Fu 9,900 piculs, Ji Feng 1,100 piculs, Ju Xing 1,800 piculs, Yu Da 2,600 piculs, He Yu 5,900 piculs, Chang Yu 1,900 piculs, Feng Tai 1,500 piculs, Shen Ji 3,400 piculs, Yong Da 1,600 piculs, and Xin Chang 2,100 piculs. The daily high and low prices are listed on the left.

Spot Cotton Selling Prices Firm and High

Spot cotton consumption is still considered good, with factories all having demand. Arrivals at the docks: Yao cotton 3,324 bales, offered at prices similar to the previous day. Tong cotton 280 bales, offered at 49.2 to 49.6 yuan.

Yao cotton 34.80 (per catty), Yong An Factory purchased 3,500 bales, weighed at the docks.

Fire Machine cotton 4.00, another 1,000 bales, spot delivery to the factory.

Another 44.00, Shen Xin Factory purchased 2,000 bales.

Lingbao cotton 3.25, Feng Tian Factory purchased 1,200 pieces.

Sha Shi cotton 20.50, Da Feng Factory purchased 56 pieces.

American Cotton Morning Buying Interest Very Strong

Yesterday, the American cotton market opened with lively and firm conditions. Prices for all months rose by four to seven points. The morning Liverpool news was good. Dealers and foreign firms bought in. Simultaneously, the trend was uncertain, and buying interest was very strong. However, as hedging sales increased, it softened again. The close was firm. Spot prices rose by one point, and futures prices rose by one to six points. British cotton spot prices were unchanged, and futures prices rose by two to three points. Indian cotton initially firmed due to short covering, but then declined due to European exporters selling Oomra and Pingguo Er. Pingguo Er fell by 0.25 rupees, Oomra rose by 0.25 rupees, and White Luoqi rose by 0.75 rupees. Telegram on the left (dated 17th).

Pingguo Er 155.50, down 0.25, 28.50

Oomra 196.75, up 0.25, 35.20

White Luoqi 120.00, up 0.75, 40.00

According to a telegram from Bombay, the opening forecast for the 18th was: White Luoqi 219.5 rupees, down 0.5 rupees; Oomra 196 rupees, down 0.75 rupees; Pingguo Er 155 rupees, down 0.5 rupees.

Osaka telegram on the 18th regarding mixed gains and losses in Sanpin yarn and cotton: Sanpin yarn futures fell by 0.1 yuan to rising by 0.5 yuan, with the near month at 216.6 yuan and the distant month at 203.9 yuan. Cotton futures rose by 0.1 yuan to falling by 0.15 yuan, with the near month at 65.25 yuan and the distant month at 64.25 yuan.

Grains: Spot Flour Bargain Sales, Flour Futures Near Weak, Far Steady

Yesterday's flour market, after the opening in the morning, showed a near weak and far steady trend for all months. Regarding foreign wheat quotes, Chicago was good by 0.23 yuan and Canada was good by 0.34 yuan. When prices were quoted, near months, due to poor actual sales, spot flour offerings, whether standard or non-standard, were all lower than the current standard market price by 0.03 to 0.05 yuan (for out-of-town customers; it would be less for those within the city). Therefore, near month prices were lower by an additional 0.01 yuan. Months below December, because foreign wheat was still good, actually rose by 0.01 yuan. When the afternoon session opened, trading turned quiet, and the market was hovering. However, this factory's flour, to cater to improved customer sales, with delivery in Tianjin, was only offered at 3.25 yuan. It was said that tens of thousands of bags were opened. Therefore, considering the actual situation, the firmness of standard flour is only swayed by sentiment.

Flour Sales Sluggish, Wheat Prices Weaken

Yesterday's wheat futures market, in the morning opening, was generally calm for all months. Because Chicago and Canada both rose by 0.02, 0.03, and 0.04 yuan, and Liverpool was down slightly, after the prices were quoted, sales for all months were not brisk, fluctuating by 0.01 yuan compared to the previous day. When the afternoon session opened, trading was brisker, and the market softened. Because spot flour sales were not active, wheat market sentiment was difficult to boost. Prices for all months fell by 0.01 to 0.02 yuan compared to the morning. The spot wheat market, high-quality goods remained stable, while medium quality goods were slightly weaker. Currently, spot flour is being offered at bargain prices privately, while the wheat market remains firm. Raw materials are expensive, and finished goods are cheap, which is quite perplexing. Shandong Yingzhou wheat opened at 5.1 yuan, down 0.05 yuan. Yao Wan wheat was 5 yuan, secondary grade 4.96 yuan. Sha He Ji wheat was 5.03 yuan. Dongtai wheat was 4.87 yuan, secondary grade 4.81 yuan. Gaoyou and Liuhe wheat were 4.9 yuan. Jiangbei wheat was 4.77 yuan, down 0.075 yuan. Shaoxing wheat was 4.09 yuan, purchased by Fu Xin at 6,000 bags and Shen Da at 1,400 bags.

Dongxin Indica Rice Arrivals Scarce, Price Increased by 0.2 Yuan

(South of Shanghai) Yesterday, shipments from various groups arrived on the 14th and 15th, totaling over 3,000 dan. Retail sales remained sluggish, with only the Qingdao group purchasing over 300 bags. Therefore, the prices of thick and thin japonica rice remained the same. However, Dongxin japonica rice lacked aroma, and prices increased by 0.2 yuan. The appearance of short-grain rice resembling new japonica rice was also tight. As shipments of Yangjian rice were abundant, sales were also sluggish, leading to a soft trend. Yinbianyuan rice maintained its normal state.

(North of Shanghai) Yesterday, shipments from various groups in Hexia were on the 41st and 42nd. Sales of various types of rice on the market were still good. Market prices were stable for broken japonica rice, thin indica rice, new customer top-grade rice, new port top-grade rice, Yinbianyuan rice. New Yangtuan and Dujian rice were firm. West japonica rice was scarce, and prices were slightly tight. Dongxin japonica rice prices increased by 0.2 yuan.

Ke Xian Rice Sales to Guangdong Resume Smoothly

Yesterday, it was said that over 20,000 bags were handled... The market immediately showed signs of improvement. Yesterday, new arrivals of Ke Xian rice were still active. The supply from the Yangtze River route was continuous. Before the Guangdong-Hankou Railway was fully open, Guangdong province's purchases were still mainly based on the Shanghai market. Yesterday, Guangdong merchants' purchasing interest was even stronger. It was said that 21,400 bags of brown rice were handled from various routes in Hankou, Jinggang, Shashi, and Nanjing. With strong sales to Guangdong, the market immediately showed signs of improvement. The Shantou group and local merchants also briskly handled Gan and Xiang machine-milled rice. The Beiyang and Yongbo groups also had a touch of 200 to 300 bags. Market sentiment was quite strong, and prices also improved by 0.04 to nearly 0.1 yuan. A total of 3,130 bags of Gan rice, 1,715 bags of Xiang machine-milled rice, 6,000 bags of rough Jinggang rice, 15,000 bags of Shashi and Hankou rice, and 100 bags of Taiwan Xian rice were opened.

Silk & Tea: Factory Prices Higher, Silk Market Transactions Less

Recently, the international silk market has been fluctuating. Yesterday, the American market opened with prices all rising sharply. Yokohama spot prices surged by 20 yuan, futures prices rose by 14 yuan, and New York's Rihua silk prices all rose by 0.03 to 0.04 yuan. The spot price for standard 20/22 denier, 7/8 evenness striped silk rose by 0.035 yuan, and the futures price rose by 0.045 yuan. As a result, local sentiment became stronger, and factory prices increased by 40 to 50 yuan, leading to smaller transactions. Yesterday, some Sichuan grey silk was sold off, and prices rose.

Recent Conditions in the Sino-American Silk Markets: US Consumption Increased Last Month, Inventories Decreased; Local Silk Market Domestic Sales Brisk, Export Sales Sluggish

Last month's US raw silk statistics report showed that consumption was 42,016 dan, an increase of over 5,300 dan compared to July. Inventories were 29,825 dan, a decrease of over 300 dan compared to the previous period, forming a situation of increased consumption and weak inventories. Based on last year's statistics (see attached table), it is projected that this month's consumption will gradually increase by 10% to 15%. As a result, sellers are unwilling to sell, so silk prices are firm, and the market is very quiet, creating opportunities for artificial silk to be active. It is heard that small merchants in New York are very interested in Shanghai 20-22 denier, yellow-white factory silk, but the quantity of this silk is not large. The Shanghai silk market, due to many speculators, is in a state of sluggish exports and brisk domestic sales. The price of 20-22 denier, 7/8 evenness striped silk has risen by about 20 to 30 yuan. It is also learned that New York bedding factories can maintain their silk usage in October and have no urgent need to purchase. Silk prices may temporarily weaken slightly.

Fine Eyebrow Pearl Tea Slightly Moving

Yesterday's green tea market was still quiet. Only Tong Fu, Bao Chang, Hua Tea, Yong Fa, and other firms in the city purchased a total of over 400 boxes of Fine Eyebrow Pearl Tea. The market price for plucked bud Fine Eyebrow has fallen to within 100 yuan, and the price for Luzhuang Pearl Tea has fallen to 70 yuan, a further decrease of 7 to 8 yuan compared to the previous period. Regarding Qimen black tea, after the Anhui-Jiangxi Black Tea General Sales Office planned to promote overall sales, Yihe, Xiehe, Jinlong, and other firms were very attentive yesterday. It is heard that telegrams have been sent, and Chinese and foreign parties are currently in negotiations.

According to a report from the Tea Industry Association, the green tea market yesterday was no different from before, and transactions were very quiet. Only various plucked bud Fine Eyebrow teas continued to have sporadic transactions by Tong Fu, Hua Tea, Bao Chang, and other firms. After Gong Xi gradually reduced its selling price, Baotou Bank's purchases were still considered uneasy, and there were quite a few transactions recently. Other Fine Eyebrow and Ping Shui teas, etc., remained silent.

Piece Goods: Demand from Various Routes Greatly Increased, Factory Cloth Insufficient for Allocation

Yesterday's cotton yarn and cotton cloth markets were both peaceful. Japanese white goods, fine cloth, fine twill, and other goods, another 2,000 pieces were opened in bulk within the last three days. Because the output number is not prosperous, the intention is very firm. Fine twill, which had been shelved, has recently seen a large increase in demand from dyeing factories, and spot goods have been completely taken away. For example, the existing stock of 300 pieces of Longtou fine twill was cleared out within three days. The Guangdong group is urging shipment of this twill very urgently. Changzhou factories' output for Guangdong orders accounts for 70%. This factory's 16-pound coarse cloth for the Yantai group, orders placed last month from Dasheng, Qingfeng, and other factories that have not yet been delivered, still amount to over 300 bags. Only a dozen bags can be allocated each day. The allocation of fancy goods is even more difficult due to the larger number of ordered items and more customers. The factories' output is limited, making allocation difficult, and the situation is worsening day by day. Customer replenishment, Tianjin group and Northwest Shaanxi group, and other assistance announced peacefully. The Guangdong group, Yunnan group, and Hankou Luzhou groups need to add additional laborers. Local merchants' sales have improved due to increased storefront business, and purchasing interest continues to be healthy. Yueque recently established a Private Inspection Committee. Yesterday, Fujian merchants stationed in Shanghai investigated various manufacturers' products for private inspection registration.

(Shark Fin Stacks) Since the customs import tax was increased from the third class to the second class, the cost of goods has been calculated to be high, and the existing stock in various stores on the market is thin. Other goods such as Silver Silk, Sanyu, and Wuyang are currently out of stock.

(Fish Maw) Arrivals from various producing areas are scarce, both new and old. Local market prices are gradually increasing. Human and Non-Human

—

From the entirety of a woman's life, it is possible to draw a vast chasm. Thus, life is divided into two parts. The first part is the virgin era, also known as the "Golden Age". During this period, like a bird in the sky, the vastness of the universe is sufficient for it to circle, the distant future fills it with endless hope, and the surrounding environment is bright, vigorous, and beautiful. The second part is the post-marriage era, with shackles and chains added layer upon layer to its body, like a bird once thrown into a net, confined to a narrow cage, suspended under a private roof. In front of it, the universe becomes narrow, the future is cut off by high walls and thick barriers. Though fortunate enough not to suffer from cold or hunger, it ultimately becomes a parasite dependent on others. When it can sing and call, and its feathers are lush, it can still be loved. But once its voice is ruined and its feathers fall out, its fate becomes uncertain.

To elaborate further, women live an upward, "human" life in the former era, while the latter era often subjects them to an irrational, almost "non-human" existence. The treatment received by women with or without knowledge is not essentially different, but women of the intellectual class experience a deeper sense of suffering. Until the remnants of feudalism and traditional concepts are completely eliminated, and the family system is reformed (breaking down large families into small families is still insufficient), this suffering will be unavoidable for most women.

When a woman is living a school life, her walk is brisk, her voice is loud, her ambitions are far-reaching, and her aspirations are grand. She refuses to show weakness to anyone, and does not easily utter a word of apology. Most of her thoughts are connected to society and the masses. This is a rational and commendable "human" life. During this period, some women with ideals and ambitions taste the experience of a non-human life, and vow to eliminate the irrational non-human life, wanting to be a female revolutionary to bring happiness to women all over the world. However, once they step into this living environment, their minds and vision are narrowed by "worldliness" and "habit," the pride of their virgin era completely disappears, and they involuntarily sink into "submission," forever unable to raise their heads!

In the world, for every man who seeks to praise women, there is an equal number of men who regard women as "objects in their palms." Are men human and women not human? Why can women only endure, submit, and live under the existing non-human conditions?

Biographies of Famous Women in the World (Continued)

— Rusabai

Karuikina and Ardusina both came from poor families. Her father was a poor peasant in the Tuva region. At the age of nine, she was doing many arduous jobs and looking after children for others. But she did not look like someone who had suffered from hunger and cold, but rather like a majestic strongman. She participated in the revolution at a young age. When she was fifteen or sixteen, working in chemical factories and textile factories, she encouraged workers to strike and vigorously promoted revolutionary work. In several domestic uprisings, she bravely went in and out of the hail of bullets to command the masses, truly worthy of being a female hero.

She is only forty years old this year, and her physique and energy are very vigorous. She is currently an alternate member of the Central Committee and serves as the secretary of the local party committee.

Although she holds important positions in the party, in order to enrich her mind and acquire abundant knowledge, she worked hard at Moscow's Sverdlov University for three years and finally achieved her goal, gaining the praise of fellow comrades in the Party Central Committee. Her future development is immeasurable.

Karuikina

Equal in prominence to alternate member Karuikina is Rosalia Zemlyachka, controller of the Soviet Union. She was born in 1876. She had already participated in the revolutionary movement before Karuikina was born, so in terms of age, among the general female revolution participants, she can be considered a veteran.

Except for the Fifth Party Congress, which she did not attend due to imprisonment, she attended every Party Congress. She served as the secretary of the Party Committee during the First Revolution in 1905 and the Second Revolution in 1917. She was a close friend of Plekhanov, Ilyich, and other pioneer revolutionaries. She worked in various places in European Russia, including St. Petersburg, Moscow, Kiev, Odessa, Ekaterinoslav, and Baku for a long time. Her reputation is above that of Kollontai and she is respected by the general public.

She is a calm and passionate person. In calm, the person's spirit is divided very finely. After the Red Army occupied Crimea, she gained fame for handling the local Crimean party counter-revolutionary base. She reorganized Crimea into the Soviet Crimea it is now. This is her greatest achievement. In short, she has a very long history in the Soviet Party. Now she is over sixty years old. Although she has no major political development in the future, as an elder of the Bolsheviks, the Federal Government expresses its respect for her and has awarded her the Red Banner and Lenin awards.

Zemlyachka

The Side Hustle of Fisherwomen on the Huangpu River

— Jiyun

People living in Shanghai probably don't know that there are such miserable women in the Huangpu River. When foreign ships dock or leave port, because the ships are huge and difficult to maneuver, it often takes a long time, two or three hours. At this time, the entire ship of passengers stands on the deck's edge, looking at relatives and friends on shore. Two or three small boats desperately row close to the ships. Most of the boats have one man and one woman, husband and wife or father and daughter, rowing long paddles with both hands, skimming across the yellow turbid water. Although they manage to row close to the ship, because the iron plate hull is smooth and impossible to climb, they are soon pushed away by the waves, and they have to continue to row closer again.

It seems like the fishing boats on the Huangpu River, but this is just a desperate side hustle. The man stands on the stern of the small boat, rowing the paddle to keep the boat from drifting away from the edge of the ship. The woman puts down the paddle and stands on the bow, holding a bamboo pole more than two fathoms long, with a small fishing net tied to the end of the pole. She uses all her strength to raise the scorching net to the edge of the deck, her face already flushed red. Swaying on the constantly rocking boat, "Hello! Money (the English word for money)!" she keeps shouting upwards, using her only English. She also frees a pair of hands, pointing at the young children on the boat, and raising her hand to her forehead, giving a salute. "Hello! Money!" Several charitable passengers throw some coins into her net. She barely endures the headache, looking up and shouting. Until the ship begins to move, she only gets a few jiao. Of course, there are also those who don't get a single cent. The woman's moaning is easier to win people's sympathy. The reason why the man rows in the back and lets the woman take on this tail-wagging, begging act is probably to exploit this psychology. But if they encounter stingy passengers, who only point and give contemptuous smiles, or take pictures of them as souvenirs of their trip to China, what can they do?

The sailors on the ship and the workers on the dock try their best to stop them because they are hindering their work. A sailor on the ship grabs her fishing net, and her body is about to be lifted into the air. The two people below bitterly plead. The sailors on the dock break their ropes or don't allow the bamboo poles to hook onto the wharf. The small boat loses its support and rocks violently. The waves crash onto the children in the middle of the boat. The paddle and bamboo pole are both lost into the water, flowing away with the waves. They struggle desperately, still trying to retrieve what they have lost. They are so angry that they have nowhere to vent, so they curse and swear arbitrarily, until those being cursed can no longer hear their voices.

Special Report by this Newspaper

A Record of Meeting Ms. Nie Lingyu

— Ji Ping

The Shanghai Public Concession is such a large area, but besides the schools of all levels run by us Chinese ourselves, the number of primary and secondary schools established by the Public Works Department is very limited. For example, there is only one girls' middle school to date, and it has only been around for five years. The Public Works Department receives tens of millions in revenue each year, and the donations and taxes paid by us Chinese naturally account for the majority. However, the amount the department spends on Chinese education is probably still less than that spent on Western education. This is very unfair! The principal of the Public Works Department Girls' Middle School, Yang Nie Lingyu, is a woman with definite experience in running schools, and I have heard people say this for a long time. The day before yesterday evening, I finally met her for the first time. We talked for a long time and visited the entire school. Now I will introduce the information I obtained to the readers:

The girls' middle school is located on Singapore Road in western Shanghai, which is a very remote place, and the transportation is not convenient. The school building is a newly built three-story Western-style building, and the style is very suitable. The site is also spacious, and it is said to be modeled after the latest German-style architecture. Indeed, the light and air are more suitable than any other school, and the interior layout is even more complete than usual. For example, in addition to fixed classrooms, there are subject-specific classrooms. Each classroom has a cloakroom attached to the back. The glass windows are specially designed so that no matter how strong the wind is, it will not blow directly on the students. Even in the severe winter season, the windows can be opened as usual, and the air will naturally not be turbid. The blackboard is light green to protect the eyes. Below it is a showcase for students of each grade to place reference books. The podium is on the left, which does not obstruct the students' view. Such a large school building is silent at night. It turns out that there are more than 500 teachers and students, none of whom live at the school. Only a few caretakers are left to guard it.

Principal Ms. Nie is a pioneer among female students who studied abroad. When she graduated from middle school, there were no women's universities in China. At that time, men and women were not allowed to attend the same school, so she had to enter the University of Michigan in the United States, first studying mathematics and physics and obtaining a master's degree. After returning to China, she taught in Jiujiang for six years, and then went to the University of Chicago to study education. After returning, she served as the principal of Nanchang Baoling Middle School. She was considered the first Chinese woman to be appointed as the principal of a church school. In 1929, she went to the United States for the third time to investigate education, and in the autumn of 1931, she was hired to her current position. Therefore, the girls' middle school was founded by her. She has several thoughts on women's education: (1) In running education, one should do practical work and not talk in high-sounding terms; (2) Adapt to the needs of society and pay attention to science education; (3) In addition to compulsory courses, new knowledge of family life should be taught; (4) In recent years, the effectiveness of women's service to society has improved compared to the past, but it is still far behind European, American, and Japanese countries. We cannot be complacent. We hope that women's professions will be more developed, but we dare not agree with improper professions; (5) The current joint examination system is too biased. Due to the physiological and psychological differences between girls and boys, they cannot take the same exam. However, the subjects of the current joint examination are the same for both men and women, which I think should be changed.

She also has many commendable points regarding student training and school management. She said that before the first class every morning, students of each grade hold an oath, which reads: "Under the guidance of teachers and the encouragement of classmates, we will study hard, abide by school rules, be diligent and endure hardship, be friendly and harmonious, cultivate the spirit of daring to be enterprising, and forge a strong and healthy body; adhere to the school motto of 'not to be served, but to serve,' shoulder the responsibility of saving the country, and advance bravely towards a bright future. We hereby swear!" After two classes, there is "civic training." The method is as follows: Each grade has a teacher responsible for discipline. Every month, all teachers and students gather in one hall to listen to the principal's speech. Every other month, the teacher answers the difficult questions raised by the students of each grade. On Wednesdays, each grade discusses specialized issues. For example, the general topic of this semester is health issues, so the discussion will not go beyond the scope of health. On Thursdays, students of each grade report on current events, dividing them into international and domestic important news. On Fridays, students give speeches, divided into Chinese and English groups. On Saturdays, famous people are invited to give speeches. This cycle repeats, giving students more extracurricular intellectual activities. As for the school management policy, there are roughly four points: (1) To cultivate students' sound physique and unique personality; (2) The students of our school all come from middle- and upper-class families, so we must train them to be leaders, so that they can go on to university or serve the society and family; (3) Home economics is important, but practical guidance is also needed on how to serve society; (4) To train them to value morality and cultivate the spirit of diligence and endurance. We dare not expect too much, but we hope to achieve our limited goals.

Ms. Nie Lingyu

Finally, she has two opinions on modern women:

(A) Cultivate a healthy body:

(1) Do not consider delicate beauty as feminine beauty

(2) Pay attention to personal hygiene, family hygiene, childbearing, and public health;

(3) Develop a balanced body and a strong physique, and then establish a good foundation in technology and knowledge.

(B) Should have a thorough awareness:

(1) Shoulder the task of national revival—uphold the spirit of mutual assistance to establish oneself and help others, and to serve society;

(2) Apply the skills learned—most urban women today are immersed in the enjoyment of pleasure, forgetting their own responsibilities. Even if they have knowledge and skills, they do not apply them in practice, completely burying themselves within the scope of the family, or submitting to the service of their husbands and children, or even indulging in dancing and banquets. This is an extreme mistake. We women should apply our skills beyond the scope of the family.

In short, we must have a spirit of hard work and cope with China's current extraordinary period, and always have the determination to sacrifice for the benefit of the public in order to realize the important task of national defense for women.

Women's Life in Taixian County

— Qiao Yunxun

Although this describes the life of women in Taixian County, it can actually include the eight counties under Yangzhou. It is one of the first places to be influenced by the Jiangnan style, but the local customs and human feelings are largely the same with minor differences. My writing about women's life in Taixian County also represents the eight counties under Yangzhou. They don't know what "women's movement" is, and those who have been educated and washed by the new tide of thought account for less than 5%. Being able to hum two lines of the seven-character verses of Liang Shanbo and Zhu Yingtai, and read two pages of the Romance of the Three Kingdoms or the Biography of Ji Gong is considered knowledgeable and courteous. They have no extravagant hopes. In their hearts and minds, they only want to win the four-character award of "exemplary mother" and "preserved female virtues" in the future, and they will be happy to smile in the afterlife. Now, let me divide it into three stages based on my imagination.

The first stage is the so-called 5% of school graduates, who mostly have only junior high school and some normal school education. They do not seek economic independence. They are pampered at home and become young mistresses when they marry. Most of them are the wives of committee members, lawyers, and young masters. Teachers are a one-in-a-thousand miracle. In short, they still cannot escape the shackles of "assisting their husbands and educating their children." They fulfill some hospitality responsibilities for their husbands' careers, which is a disguised form of domestic help. With spare time, the young mistress of the Zhang mansion attends some aimless banquets, playing mahjong eight rounds with each other, and mostly spend their years in this way.

The second stage of women have fairly wealthy families. Managing household affairs and raising children are the main duties of these women. Washing clothes, cooking, and fetching water are done by a maid. Young women follow their mother-in-law and assist in trivial household chores. Middle-aged women manage finances, and sometimes play a game or two of mahjong or cards for fun. Elderly women in this second stage are diligent and thrifty, taking care of tea and rice, and looking after the seven necessities of life. Otherwise, they chant Buddhist scriptures and take care of themselves in their old age. Some, who are more absurd, are addicted to small gambling dens.

The women in the third stage are the poorest and can represent the general life of women. Washing clothes, cooking rice and porridge, raising sons and daughters, sweeping the floor and wiping the table are all done by themselves. In short, the women here live under the shadow of "a husband's glory, a wife's nobility, and a pampered child." The families I am talking about are naturally not rich enough. They don't make their own needles, but help others sew clothes. During this transition of seasons, their only side job is to make nets. This handicraft is rarely found in Jiangnan. the yarn with great effort and hardship, they twist it first. Then, make it a line, and then, twist it into a thread. The surgery is very hot, and one can twist one feet a day. One yuan of capital can get three yuan of goods price. The clothing and food support is not not complement. The operation is watched on a star and eye! The spirit of taste must not be tolerated! This can only get to the micro profit.

What I Learned from Interviewing Working Women: The Thoughts and Lives of Female Employees at the New Asia Hotel

— Xian Ying

In recent years, the advancement of women's occupations in the country has shown a very rapid surge. Initially, most were primary school teachers and female workers in factories. Then, government agencies and commercial society gradually had female employees. Therefore, the investigation of the lives and the examination of the thoughts of those professional women have become a new and interesting job. What I want to describe here can be said to be the newest of many kinds of women's occupations. Perhaps two broad and extremely developed new paths are where women's occupations can be most effective in the future, that is, the hotel business.

On a late summer afternoon, I drove to the mysterious head of North Sichuan Road. That long snake-like row of red houses is now in front of me. In my casual wandering, I found a special job, that is, I wanted to visit a few female employees in that New Asia Hotel this afternoon.

Women becoming employees in the hotel business may still be rare in China, but in foreign countries, on the one hand, because of the development and importance of the hotel business, and on the other hand, because of the recognition of women's unique strengths—carefulness, harmony, patience, etc.—which are more suitable for the position of hotel clerk, women have already created a special position in the hotel business. For example, the book "Women in Hotel Business" emphasizes that women should run the hotel business, and concludes that "I believe that in a few years, women will dominate the business that they should dominate." It may well be possible!

Among the hotels completely run by ourselves in our country, the New Asia Hotel is definitely second to none. Manager Zhong Biao can be said to be a "national expert" in hotels. Under his management, the New Asia Hotel emphasizes the use of female employees as an important policy. Therefore, he has now hired more than a dozen female workers, who are distributed on each floor to specialize in rough work such as wiping floors, wiping windows, washing, and tidying up. As for the female employees, they are all on the ground floor, and can be roughly divided into four departments:

1. Information desk: Three information clerks in light red Western-style uniforms

2. Elevator operators: Four elevator operators in light green Western-style uniforms

3. Chinese restaurant waitresses: Six waitresses in light green uniforms with white aprons

4. Telephone switchboard operators: Six telephone switchboard operators, plus one in the cloakroom, for a total of four departments with twenty people. What I have learned from my visit now is only a case study of five representatives selected from each of their departments, those five:

Information desk - Miss Bao Mali

Elevator desk - Miss Chen Yuping

Chinese restaurant - Miss Zhang Peiyi

Telephone switchboard - Miss Su Xiuzhen

Chinese restaurant and elevator - Miss Chen Xiuqin

Their similarities are:

(1) They are all of Cantonese origin, and have been in Shanghai for many years, and can speak extremely fluent Cantonese, ordinary Mandarin, and English.

(2) The ages are all around twenty years old, differing by one or two years. Except for Mali, all are unmarried.

(3) The salary is between 40 and 50 yuan per month, and it is not regarded as the only income for their families. (To be continued)

Old Clothes

—

The sky seemed to have encountered some sad event, crying there all day and night, for almost three days in a row. If it continues like this, there will inevitably be a year of flood and drought. The price of rice has risen to 18 yuan, 20 yuan per dan, and the price of tofu has also risen, and the price of meat has also risen. These are all unavoidable!

Wei Qing sat in the small accounting room, which was as narrow as the bottom of an escalator, looking at the sky, thinking very absentmindedly, thinking of these terrible predictions. He really couldn't continue to calculate the batch of accounts that the manager had just given him. However, the rising prices of rice and meat are still future changes, and for the time being, he can still force himself not to think about them. What is difficult is that he remembers his son Da Bao when he left home in the morning. Rui Zhu told him that Da Bao only had a decent set of clothes, which he had been wearing for a week. It was really too dirty. If he wore it to school again, it would be too embarrassing to wash it overnight. How easy is it to dry on a rainy day? So it is best to teach Wei Qing to discuss with his brother-in-law Yu Daishan to ask for one or two clean old clothes to change. Yes, the Yu family has been making a lot of money recently! I remember the last time Rui Zhu's sister, Li Zhu, brought her eldest son, Xue Ling, to Wei Qing's house, she was dressed so exquisitely! According to their accompanying servants, this child had twenty or thirty pieces of seasonal clothing in his wardrobe! And Da Bao's figure happened to be about the same as Xue Ling's, so Rui Zhu's idea of ​​coming up with this emergency solution was really very clever. However, Wei Qing thought: I can't afford to make new clothes for my son, but I go to ask people for old clothes to wear. It's really embarrassing. It's best not to go. Then buy new ones. Although it is said that there are no new ones worth two or three yuan, there are also not that much new clothes and there are only eighteen days left until the end of the month. There are only eleven yuan left at home. How can he spend such an extra sum? He planned like this for a long time, and finally he still took the rain to Yu's house, and under Rui Zhu's very embarrassing begging, he got two old clothes.

It was seven fifteen when he got home. Rui Zhu, Da Bao, Xi Chang, and Xiao Luo were all holding rice bowls and waiting for him. As soon as Rui Zhu saw him coming with a paper bag, she shouted with a happy expression:

"Okay! Da Bao's new clothes are here!"

Opening the paper bag, Da Bao also smiled. It turned out that all of Da Bao's own clothes were always made of cheap foreign cloth, and the styles were very old. But today, the two old clothes that Wei Qing had asked for from Yu's house were all wool, and the workmanship was exquisite, and the styles were good-looking. Da Bao felt that they were much better than the new clothes made at his own house!

Wei Qing and Rui Zhu were naturally very happy to see Da Bao happy, especially Xi Chang and Xiao Luo, the two younger siblings, were overjoyed.

The next day, Da Bao went to school, and the teacher and classmates couldn't help but take a few more glances at him. Da Bao thought in his heart that this must be because of the new clothes, and he was so happy that he couldn't be better. From then on, whether he went to school or went to the park with his father, he didn't want to wear his own clothes anymore. He had to wear the two old clothes that he had asked for from Yu's house. But if anyone asked, he always said that they were made at home, and he repeatedly told his father and mother not to tell people that they were borrowed.

Unfortunately, one day, at another relative's house, Da Bao and Xue Ling met. Xue Ling's memory was really good. As soon as he saw Da Bao, he pulled on his clothes and laughed:

"These are my old clothes! Your father came to ask us for them!"

Hearing him say this, Da Bao felt that everyone around him was laughing at him. His little face turned as red as if it had been dyed, and he finally ran to Rui Zhu's side and cried. Rui Zhu also seemed to hear people quietly saying "old clothes are borrowed", "no wonder they don't fit", "turns out they are picked up old clothes"... Under the emotion of shame and anger. The helpless mother had to escape with her poor son.

Supplement to the Local News Section of the Shen Bao

Spiritual Blessing and Simple Questions

—Answered by Physician Liu Bo

Advice for Seeking Medical Consultation

1. The letter should be written in plain language.

2. Do not use vague 'disease names' like "wind," "cold," "fire," or incomprehensible and non-specific terms.

3. Please include postage in your letter: 5 cents for out-of-town, 2 cents for local. Letters deemed lacking in public value by the enemy, and those where the patient prefers a private response, will be answered directly via return mail.

4. Please clearly state the patient's detailed address.

5. Send letters to our clinic: 1108 Qinyuan Village, Xinwen Road, Shanghai.

6. Medical consultations are free of charge.

7. If asking about two diseases in one letter, or several aspects of one disease—such as causes, symptoms, diagnosis, prognosis, and treatment—please number them.

8. Consultations are limited to internal medicine and dermatology/venereology.

9. This column will publicly answer questions every Saturday.

Dizziness and Brain Fog

Twenty-Ninth Query, Mr. Jiang Wei, 38 Yufei Lane, North Sichuan Road asks: Due to my job, I have to sleep between 12:00 AM or 2:00 AM to 4:00 AM every day and get up at 8:00 AM. This lifestyle lasted for four years. Now, I have been away from this lifestyle for four months, but I have become a neurasthenic. Every day after getting up, I feel dizzy and have brain fog all day long. When I shake my head, my brain makes "kak, kak, kak" sounds. When I read a little more, my brain becomes even more confused—like having a fever. At the same time, my eyes also feel tired. These symptoms started three years ago, but they were very mild at the time. I have taken several Western medicines, but none of them have worked. There are capitalists in this day and age who only care about stuffing piles of banknotes into their safes and depositing them in banks, and do not hesitate to harm promising young people; it is truly infuriating. Not to boast, but in my childhood, I suffered even more economic and personal hardships than you. Although recovery is not as fast as with other diseases, I can guarantee that it will be greatly reduced after eight months. During this recovery period, you should pay attention to not reading, and not worrying about your illness and other things. (3) There is no danger to life. Your illness will get better, absolutely get better, don't worry too much about it! (4) Everything you like to eat is beneficial for your illness, especially egg yolk. (5) Use some "magnesium carbonate" for dry application.

Discussions

The Consistent Hope of the People

— Yi Wo

Since the founding of the Republic of China, it can be said that there has not been a single day of peace. It has either been a time of internal strife or external aggression. The difficulty of such times can be described as sitting on pins and needles, or having thorns in one's back, unable to rest peacefully. However, to avoid the attack of external disasters, we must first strengthen our defenses and clear the fields, and organize internal affairs. This is the consistent view of our people, and it is also the only way to reorganize the country, which no one can deny.

Unexpectedly, the abnormal movements of Guangdong and Guangxi, under the guise of external defense, first called themselves armies. Fortunately, the central authorities saw through this point and were determined not to deal with them by force, but first showed sincerity, opened their hearts, and appealed to them with righteousness, clarifying the fortune and misfortune. Naturally, warlords who specialize in extortion were abandoned by their followers and collapsed without a fight. The serious situation in the Southwest, where the mountains were about to collapse and the wind filled the building, melted away like ice and snow in less than two months. Peace prevailed. This was the government's established national policy, and it was also the consistent hope of the people. Removing a source of disaster means preserving some vitality for the country. This is the first hope of our people.

With the departure of the Chen faction, Li and Bai remained. Although Guangdong had already submitted to the central government, Guangxi Province was still unable to unify. The central government spared no effort to compromise and sent senior officials to negotiate cooperation, and declared that it would never deal with them by force, but would use political means to persuade them. Li and Bai's contribution lay in the Republic of China, governing one province, and the righteousness was obvious, not to be refuted. Naturally, in a peaceful atmosphere, the situation of estrangement and obstruction that had existed for years was completely eliminated. In this way, not only did the country achieve the effect of peaceful unification, but it also gained the help of its limbs. This is the second hope of our people.

With the country unified, we can talk about diplomacy. Yue came to Beijing to discuss the overall situation. The name of the incident was the Chengdu Incident, but in reality, it sought to adjust the entire diplomacy. The entire negotiation and the entire adjustment were certainly welcome. Before we understand what kind of method and what kind of conditions will be used for the adjustment, it is not appropriate to judge it. However, we know that the visit of Ambassador Chuan Yue this time had a great mission and was not comparable to ordinary envoys. It is said that the Japanese authorities regarded the Chengdu Incident as a serious matter, so before Ambassador Chuan Yue came to China, the Japanese foreign, land, and naval ministers held emergency meetings many times to discuss countermeasures. Prime Minister Hirota and Foreign Minister Arita also met with the Emperor several times to report on the progress and countermeasures in handling this matter. The importance they attach to this matter is evident.

In fact, the Chengdu mass riot incident was not very serious. The details of this matter remain to be thoroughly investigated. The truth has not yet been clarified. In short, this incident was nothing more than a manifestation of the unstable situation in the Chengdu area, and unfortunately, a Japanese journalist was brutally killed during this period. Therefore, I believe that if the Japanese authorities truly want to achieve amity, they should not make a mountain out of a molehill, and should uphold the principle of turning big things into small things and small things into nothing, and discuss them peacefully and calmly in public. Perhaps this can achieve the true effect of friendship. Otherwise, the situation will become more rigid, and our country's endurance of compromise will probably have reached its limit. This is the third hope of our people.

Tragedy in the Villa

— Yi Yi

Because it was already late when we left that small inn, we were overtaken by the hot sun when the car drove to Kaiyuan Temple. It was as if thousands of large furnaces were placed around us. "If we have to walk like this for a day, we'll turn into dried shrimp!" The old driver kept wiping his sweat and shouting. But there was something even more interesting happening: the old driver even took off his pants. He pointed to the white flesh below his stomach, which was out of sync with the rest of his body, and said, "...Hey, sir, look, even a young girl's flesh probably isn't as tender as mine!" After he said that, we all burst out laughing, and the laughter was immediately swallowed by the silence of the wilderness.

"Aren't you afraid of running into someone?"

"People? ...Hmph, don't worry, sir,

Page 20

You won't run into any women. What kind of woman would dare to walk in this boundless wilderness! If they run into young lads! Hahahaha... that account won't be settled... Giddy up! Whoa! ...Don't you think so! ...If we run into men, what's so rare about that? Wouldn't a laugh settle everything? ...If you can't stand the heat, you should take off your pants too. Let me tell you, sir! Politeness isn't worth anything in the countryside—if you wear a long gown and mandarin jacket, or some Western suit and tie, you might get heatstroke and go back to your grandma's!"

The horse was panting, and slowly walked forward.

It seemed that the vast land was like a round millstone. Although we were moving forward, we always seemed to be standing still in the center of the millstone. It wasn't us moving, but the land that was spinning.

"Hey! That hillside over there is Qilibao! The only villa I was talking about is on the left of the fort," the old driver said to me, gazing ahead and turning his head halfway.

"Weren't you going to tell me about the fort? I've been holding back the punchline." "Well then, you can tell it now, okay?"

"What's so bad about that?..." So he coughed twice, whipped the horse twice, and the story began like this:

"Ahem! ...Rich people always have a lot of things to deal with. They're full, they've had enough to drink, they have nothing to do, and boring things follow!

The owner of that villa was in his fifties. I've even met him. He was very strong. He had never been an official. He lived a very comfortable life thanks to his ancestors' estate. He always went on a trip once a year, and that would take a month or two.

His wife was said to be very young, only in her twenties. Some people say she was his concubine, but I don't know! In short, their relationship wasn't very good, tch! There was always something going on! ...Hahaha...!

It was probably, ...uh, that's right, it was in the autumn seven years ago. The gentleman had just returned from Qingdao, where he had gone to escape the summer heat, and that's when the tragic events gradually unfolded.

The reason was that the gentleman had brought back from Qingdao...

...What? ...Haha, the nature of that relationship doesn't need me to explain! The old gentleman spent every day with that girl and had long thrown his wife to the four winds! ...Hmph! The wife didn't like the old man, but the old man treated that girl so well, which aroused her jealousy and resentment. Isn't that right? For about the first month, they argued several times every day. The old gentleman always protected that girl and found many reasons to make things difficult for his wife. Several times, the old gentleman even hit his wife.

The rift between them deepened day by day.

One night, suddenly the old gentleman's beloved girl died, her whole body turning blackish-purple and covered with spots, and blood flowed from her mouth, nostrils, and other places. The old gentleman was desperate. He knew who had caused her death. By the time he picked up his gun and rushed to his wife's room, she had already disappeared. His mind lost control, and he fired his gun aimlessly, killing two servants and a maid. So... he then went... somewhere. Sometimes he would laugh... sometimes he would wail... sometimes he would say things that no one else could understand, running through every house in Qilibao looking for something! ...Alas! ...

After making such a fuss for less than a month, the poor old gentleman also disappeared, but he was found less than a week later. He was found dead in a mud puddle less than two miles from Qilibao! ...".

"Hey! ...Look!" The old driver raised his voice and pointed to a small white house hidden behind a belt of pine trees. "...That's the villa! ...Do you see it, sir! ..."

My heart was being bitten by something. I nodded!

"It's said that it's haunted at night! ...No one dares to pass by there at night! ..." The old driver said with some bluster.

"Is the fort lively?" I asked him.

"Um! ...It's still a second-class small town. There are shops and everything. We can have lunch there... Oh! ..." He stopped the horse and burst out laughing! I asked him why he stopped the car, and he said, smiling, "I almost made a mistake. If I had entered the fort with my bare ass, I would have been beaten to a pulp! ..."

So he put on his pants.

Old Russian Street

— Luo Peng

In the early morning, pushing open the window, a gust of cool wind came, making me shiver involuntarily. Only then did I realize that autumn had arrived in the human world. The sky was gloomy. The leaves of the several mulberry trees outside the window, which had been a dense, yellowish green just a few days ago, were curled up, and one by one they began to fall from their branches, drifting and rolling in the sky and on the ground, like windmills.

I leaned on the window sill, lit a cigarette, and gazed at the empty square outside the window, filled with fine stones and broken tiles: A few days ago, there were crooked huts here, but they were forcibly demolished yesterday. In the distance, there were also a few equally dilapidated huts, scattered next to several high-rise buildings. Thinking about their future fate, I felt a sense of desolation.

I don't know when, a fine drizzle started to fall outside the window, as fine as spiderwebs. Although it didn't have the grandeur of a downpour, its power was not small: In a moment, the square was covered in mud, and puddles formed in the low-lying areas. Some dogs were listlessly squatting by the wall, their heads lowered to the ground, motionless, their large, sorrowful eyes wide open, rain dripping slowly from their heads, as if they were weeping. In a corner of the square, there were even a few puppies mournfully whimpering, intermittently, like Buddhist monks and Taoist priests blowing summoning horns in the dead of night.

The streetlights were bright, the drizzle fell even denser, and my stomach felt a little hungry. I didn't know how I had gotten through this day. Suddenly, I remembered Old Russian Street; every day when I went to the restaurant, I had to pass by there. I wondered how those White Russians who had been exiled to a foreign land were doing. Some might be hiding under other people's eaves, or perhaps they had drunk their fill of cheap liquor, numbly collapsed in the soggy mud, or were wandering the streets like stray dogs.

Crossing the square outside the window, I reached Old Russian Street. In fact, it was a dark and narrow alley where groups of White Russian men and women gathered; the patrol officers didn't often come here. Therefore, the waiters and shop assistants in those shops called this alley Old Russian Street.

I didn't carry an umbrella or wear a raincoat, and hurriedly ran there. I stood at the entrance of Old Russian Street. Under the street light stood a White Russian woman, the dim light shining on her pale face. Her thin, elongated body was enveloped in a loose, tattered overcoat. I recognized her. This woman asked me for a cigarette every night.

Page 21

"Hello!" She walked closer to me again: "Cigarettes," she said, moving her index finger. I quickly gave her a cigarette. She lit the cigarette and went back to her original spot.

Every night, after I gave her a cigarette, I would walk away, my body trembling. I didn't dare look at her too much. Tonight, I mustered up the courage to stand there.

Look! She threw the cigarette butt on the ground, and then hurriedly ran towards me, stepping wildly in the mud, splashing mud on my face; I panicked, wishing I could turn around and run. But unexpectedly, the woman passed by me, picked up a puppy squatting by the wall at the entrance of the street, tucked it into her arms, and walked towards the other end of Old Russian Street.

After taking only a few steps, she turned her head and glanced at me, closing her eyes and smiling, a lascivious smile! I ignored her and continued to stand there. She probably felt disappointed and sat down next to a group of White Russian men and women in the corner of the wall near her. They took turns smoking cigarettes, all silent, unable to say a word, letting the rain soak their bodies.

My stomach rumbled loudly with hunger, and the rain flowed down from my head, the cool breeze brushing my face, making it a little unbearable. But I didn't know if I felt sadness or anger? Standing there, I couldn't speak for a long time.

Old Foreigner

— Lin Na

From the second-class carriage of the 10:30 train from Davao, the old foreigner Chen Jinsui, carrying a suitcase, hurriedly squeezed out onto the platform. He was as fat and plump as a boar, and he panted as he walked. After leaving the platform, he put down the suitcase in his hand, took out a handkerchief to wipe the sweat off his face, and waved his hand far away like he was hailing a carriage. The coachman cleverly raised the long whip in his hand and shouted, urging the horse to come over.

"74 Pasig Road," the old foreigner jumped in and shouted angrily.

The coachman nodded meekly, whistling softly. The whip swirled in the air and then silently fell on the thin back of the horse, and the carriage began to move slowly. He looked around with disgust and then sank back into his uneasy thoughts. Three days ago, in Davao, he received a letter from a friend in Manila, talking about his daughter studying in Manila, so he rushed over. Now he felt very depressed and kept muttering to himself:

"No wonder she kept saying she was busy preparing for her studies and didn't come back to Davao for three holidays." After thinking for a while, he continued, "Then how should I tell her? I should tell her everything I know, and then angrily question her: Do you think you can hide it from me? Do you have anything else to say about this disgraceful matter? Why did I send you to Manila to go to university? You know it was for the honor of the overseas Chinese community, the honor of the Chen family. Now you have humiliated the Chen family and the entire overseas Chinese community. Do you have anything to say? No? Good, come back to Davao with me..."

He smiled, feeling very satisfied with his arrangement. During the day and night journey, he had been thinking about these words. He believed in his success.

"What will she do then?" he thought. "Surely, she will run in front of me, her eyes filled with tears, sobbing softly: — I... I was young and didn't know what I was doing, Dad, please forgive me! ... And me? I will sigh, gasping for breath: — I will forgive you, forgive you, child..."

The carriage jolted quickly, turned down a street, and then continued smoothly. The sun was listlessly shining on the hot asphalt road. The sound of horseshoes hitting the road was crisp and clear, vibrating in the silent street, and then disappearing into the hot, stuffy sky!

Suddenly, a sharp thought pierced into his mind! "What if she resists?" He was very surprised, as if a prisoner had suddenly discovered that he was about to be executed: "Then, I will exercise the rights given to me by the law. I will appeal to the Supreme Court and sue the young man who is studying at the university and chasing after her. I will use justice to convince her: Think about it, a noble Chinese woman marrying this barbaric, uncivilized native, wouldn't that humiliate the entire overseas Chinese community? Wouldn't that humiliate the glory of our Chen family? For the sake of our glory and for the sake of your future, give him up, abandon him. There are plenty of well-off and wealthy Chinese men... Wouldn't her heart be moved by this? Yes, she will change her mind..."

The carriage was traveling along a quiet street. The coachman kept looking at the conspicuous house numbers on both sides with his two black, golden eyes, constantly muttering, "Twenty-four, twenty-six, twenty-eight..."

Finally, he pulled the reins tightly, and the horse raised its head in fright, stomping its front hooves. After a moment, it stopped, drooping its sweaty head in frustration. The coachman then turned back to him and smiled slightly, "Sir, number 74 has arrived!"

The old foreigner leaned out and looked around. In front of him stood a row of neat little Western-style houses, the number 74 sign in blue and white smiling conspicuously at him. He paid the fare, jumped out, and strode in. In the parlor, a man dressed as a servant greeted him. He told him the surname of the person he was looking for and was led upstairs.

In a room with a certain surname written on it, he gently reached out and knocked. A Eurasian woman came out and opened the door for him. Then, a clear sound of the piano floated towards him. He stepped inside, feeling slightly displeased. This was a fairly well-decorated room. The flowered wallpaper on the walls and the curtains hanging in front of the windows made him a little dizzy. A woman in a nightgown was sitting in front of a piano, playing a choral piece. Not far from her, a dark-skinned young gentleman was sitting on a sofa chair, with a plump child of about one year old sitting on his lap, babbling and waving two small hands.

The old foreigner was a little surprised. He stopped abruptly, thinking that he had entered the wrong room. However, he quickly dismissed this suspicion. The woman who was playing the piano had already stood up and was facing him, revealing a timid and uneasy expression, and said to him in a low voice in English: "Dad..."

The gentleman sitting on the sofa also stood up abruptly with the child in his arms. He was a little flustered, but still wore a restrained smile on his face.

Before she had time to introduce them, he understood everything. He felt neither resentment nor despair. What was in front of him was an irreversible fact. What else could he say? He could only quietly...

Page 22

"You've both done well, don't worry, child, I came here specifically to see you..."

His tears welled up and fell.

Ordinary Trivialities

— Liang Qiyun

My beloved Xian Boqing lost his job. — That was because the rubber factory went bankrupt.

The witch and matchmaker Xu Erguniang prayed to the Western Marquis King Bodhisattva for him.

"The Western Marquis King is efficacious. Half of my life has been blessed by the King. Didn't Gao Lao Chen Dehui's eldest son and crippled Tan get a job about a week or so after they prayed... Xu Erguniang's... like this... to Xian..."

And the result was very interesting: The unemployed rubber shoe factory worker frowned even tighter; Xu Erguniang was happy as if she had won several rounds of "Five Hundred."

On a drizzly autumn night, my beloved finally went back to his hometown with his family, frowning...

About three weeks after they left, the owner of the room that the worker lived in changed to a young couple. But, according to them, they had not yet been married.

The man was an elementary school teacher, with a small harmonium. In the quiet dusk, the harmonium's sob often accompanied an aged and melancholy low voice —

"Do you know how long life is!

You are still young,

Why hang your face like an old weeping willow!

Let me see: your

Eyes are not full of the vitality of life!

Just like that, live on." (To be continued)

Movies

On the Performance of the Chinese Translation of "The Fatherland"

Today, Mr. Tang Huaiqiu leads the China Traveling Theatre Troupe in the premiere of the five-act historical drama "The Fatherland" (Patrie), originally written by Victorien Sardou, at the Carlton Theater. The play was successfully previewed last Monday, as noted in this newspaper.

Although we ourselves cannot fully appreciate the beauty and goodness of Mr. Chen Mian's translation, everything leads us to believe that his translation is very good, because Mr. Chen Mian is not only a national doctorate in our country (this degree is already a valuable guarantee, worthy of our respect), but also a literary scholar and practitioner. He has translated "Le Cid," and scholars who are fluent in both Chinese and French have praised it. If he can overcome the difficulty of translating such poetic and literary works, then translating this prose "The Fatherland" will be much easier for him.

Mr. Chen Mian's hard work is not only satisfied with providing the translation of French dramas to their literary scholars, but also strives to realize these dramas on the Chinese stage. He cleverly writes to hope that the characters in the play will move on stage in front of the public, whether with joy or sorrow.

He found a proud collaborator in Mr. Tang Huaiqiu. The two complement each other, Mr. Chen Mian chose the play and translated it, and Mr. Tang Huaiqiu performed it.

Choosing a script is a difficult and delicate task. A tragedy or comedy cannot be welcomed by Chinese audiences simply because it is a masterpiece in its own country. There is a gap between Chinese drama and French or European drama.

When Mr. Chen Mian translated "Andromaque," he knew that he could not hope for the performance of this translation. The distance between Chinese flesh and ancient European history is too far, so it is difficult to be interested in plays with this theme, although Racine has renewed the ancient text. Furthermore, in this play, Racine's subtle descriptions of psychology require a lot of effort to be truly appreciated by Far Easterners, and this effort can only be done by people of special classes. (To be continued)
